8.1 μs

Mitochondrial Genome Phylogency

This notebook tries to replicate a result from [1] where the autors used the Normalized Compression Distance to calculate pairwaise distaces between the mitochondrial DNA of various animals and then uses these distances to create a phylogenetic tree.

15.8 μs

Note

The results here might be slightly different from the paper as we do not use the exact same string compressors, and the algorithm used to reconstruct the phylogenetic tree might also be slightly different.

30.4 μs

Setup

We load a bunch of packages, this might take a while...

8.1 μs
91.5 s
11.9 s

We start by loading the mitochondiral DNA of 20 different animals from nuccore. Using the efetch function from BioServices.jl this is a very easy thing to do, one has just to know the correct sequence id for each animal.

Calculating pairwise distances

The Normalized Compressor Distance uses a loseless string compressor - changing the compressor should have an influence on the quality of the result.

For comparison we also use the Levenshtein Distance which is provided by StringDistances.jl. Calculating this istance might need a few minutes.

20.0 μs

Tip

When viewing the static html version of this notebook it might not be possible to choose another distance - try running the interactive notebook instead.

We can now calulate all pairwise distances and visualize the matrix. As close animal groups are already next to each other in the input list, we can immediately spot some clusters.

Creating a phylogenetic tree

Finally, we can pass the distance matrix to the nj! function from PhyloNetworks.jl to create a phylogenetic tree and then plot this tree using PhyloPlots.jl.

18.0 μs
5.9 s
